Create a new branch from `main` named `release/vX.Y.Z` (e.g. `release/v1.0.0`).\n    28→2. Update the CHANGELOG.md with the release notes for the new version. (We have a `mage` task to help with this in the `build` directory.)\n    29→3. Commit the changes and push the branch to GitHub.\n    30→4. Create a pull request from the release branch to `main`.\n    31→5. Once the pull request is merged, create a new tag on `main` with the version number (e.g. `v1.0.0`).\n    32→6. The artifacts can then be downloaded and tested.\n    42→\n    43→### Nightly Releases\n    44→\n    45→Nightly releases are created automatically every night at 23:30 UTC via the [Nightly Release GitHub Action](.github/workflows/nightly.yml).\n    46→\n    47→The nightly release also does not create an actual release. Unlike the snapshot release, the nightly release does not upload the binaries as artifacts. Instead, the nightly release builds a Docker image and pushes it to Docker Hub and GitHub Container Registry (Linux arm and x64 only). The release process builds the binary for each platform and uploads them to the [Flipt GitHub Releases page](https://github.com/flipt-io/flipt/releases).\n\nWe also publish a Docker image for each release to [Docker Hub](https://hub.docker.com/r/flipt/flipt/tags) and [GitHub Container Registry](https://github.com/flipt-io/flipt/pkgs/container/flipt).\n\n## Release Process\n\nWe use GitHub Actions and [GoReleaser Pro](https://goreleaser.com/) to build and publish Flipt releases.\n\nWe support three main types of releases:\n\n- Stable releases (e.g. `v1.0.0`)\n- Snapshot releases (e.g. `v1.0.0-snapshot`)\n- Nightly releases (e.g. `v1.0.0-nightly`)\n\nThe process for each looks roughly the same using GitHub Actions and GoReleaser Pro, but there are some differences in how the release is tagged and how the release is published.\n\n![Release Process](.github/images/release-process.png)\n\n### Stable Releases\n\n1. Create a new branch from `main` named `release/vX.Y.Z` (e.g. `release/v1.0.0`).\n2. Update the CHANGELOG.md with the release notes for the new version. (We have a `mage` task to help with this in the `build` directory.)\n3. Commit the changes and push the branch to GitHub.\n4. Create a pull request from the release branch to `main`.\n5. Once the pull request is merged, create a new tag on `main` with the version number (e.g. `v1.0.0`).\n6. Push the tag to GitHub.\n7. CI will build and publish the release to GitHub and Docker Hub.\n\n### Snapshot Releases\n\nSnapshot releases are created on-demand and are used to test the build and release process for stable releases.\n\nTo create a snapshot release, we run the [Snapshot Release GitHub Action](.github/workflows/snapshot.yml) workflow manually from the GitHub Actions UI.\n\nThe snapshot release does not create an actual release, it simply builds the binaries and uploads them as artifacts to the workflow run. The artifacts can then be downloaded and tested.\n\n### Nightly Releases\n\nNightly releases are created automatically every night at 23:30 UTC via the [Nightly Release GitHub Action](.github/workflows/nightly.yml).\n\nThe nightly release also does not create an actual release. Unlike the snapshot release, the nightly release does not upload the binaries as artifacts. Instead, the nightly release builds a Docker image and pushes it to Docker Hub and GitHub Container Registry (Linux arm and x64 only). The Docker image is tagged with the version number (e.g. `v1.0.0-nightly`).\n\nCurrently the nightly release only builds the Docker image for Linux. We do not build a nightly release for macOS.\n","numLines":50,"startLine":1,"totalLines":50}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01YaLDijgUCesLNCP2yasqDd","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01ABwwPKRktJZJmuS5y2a2uk","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/RELEASE_NOTES.md","content":"# Flipt Release Notes\n\n## Overview\n\nThis release introduces significant improvements to OpenTelemetry (OTEL) tracing instrumentation, providing better observability and more granular control over trace sampling and propagation.\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\nNone. This is a backward-compatible release.\n\n## New Features\n\n### Tracing Configuration Enhancements\n\n#### Sampling Ratio Configuration\n- **`tracing.samplingRatio`**: New configuration option to control the fraction of traces to sample.\n  - Type: `number` (float64)\n  - Range: `0.0` to `1.0`\n  - Default: `1` (sample 100% of traces)\n  - Example configuration:\n    ```yaml\n    tracing:\n      enabled: true\n      exporter: jaeger\n      samplingRatio: 0.1  # Sample 10% of traces\n    ```\n  - **Migration Path**: If you upgrade from a previous version and want to reduce trace overhead, set this value to less than 1. For example, `0.1` will sample only 10% of traces.\n\n#### Trace Propagators Configuration\n- **`tracing.propagators`**: New configuration option to specify OpenTelemetry text map propagators for distributed tracing.\n  - Type: `array` of strings\n  - Default: `[\"tracecontext\", \"baggage\"]`\n  - Supported values:\n    - `tracecontext` - W3C Trace Context propagator\n    - `baggage` - W3C Baggage propagator\n    - `b3` - Zipkin B3 Single propagator\n    - `b3multi` - Zipkin B3 Multi propagator\n    - `jaeger` - Jaeger propagator\n    - `xray` - AWS X-Ray propagator\n    - `ottrace` - OpenTracing propagator\n    - `none` - No-op propagator\n  - Example configuration:\n    ```yaml\n    tracing:\n      enabled: true\n      exporter: jaeger\n      propagators:\n        - tracecontext\n        - baggage\n        - jaeger  # Add Jaeger propagation support\n    ```\n  - **Use Case**: Enable multiple propagators when your traces need to be compatible with different trace collection systems or when propagating traces across systems using different standards.\n\n### Enhanced Tracing Resource Information\n\nTracing spans now include more semantic information from OpenTelemetry semantic conventions v1.24.0:\n- **Service Information**: Service name (`flipt`) and version\n- **Container Information**: Container ID, image name, and other container metadata (when running in containers)\n- **Host Information**: Hostname, OS type, and architecture\n- **Runtime Information**: Go runtime version, runtime name, and description\n- **Telemetry SDK Information**: Information about the OpenTelemetry SDK version being used\n- **Environment Variables**: Automatic detection of OTEL environment variables\n\n## Configuration Guide\n\n### Sampling Configuration Example\n\nTo reduce trace overhead in production while maintaining high sampling in development:\n\n```yaml\nversion: \"1.0\"\n\ntracing:\n  enabled: true\n  exporter: jaeger\n  jaeger:\n    host: localhost\n    port: 6831\n  # Sample only 10% of traces in production\n  samplingRatio: 0.1\n  # Use standard W3C propagators\n  propagators:\n    - tracecontext\n    - baggage\n```\n\n### Multi-Propagator Configuration Example\n\nFor integrations with multiple observability systems:\n\n```yaml\ntracing:\n  enabled: true\n  exporter: otlp\n  otlp:\n    endpoint: localhost:4317\n  # Support multiple trace formats\n  propagators:\n    - tracecontext    # W3C standard\n    - baggage         # W3C baggage\n    - jaeger          # Jaeger format\n    - b3multi         # Zipkin format\n```\n\n## Configuration Validation\n\nThe configuration now validates:\n- **Sampling Ratio**: Must be a number between 0 and 1 (inclusive)\n- **Propagators**: Must be valid propagator names from the supported list\n\nInvalid configurations will result in a clear error message at startup.\n\n## Upgrade Guide\n\n### For Users Not Using Tracing\n\nNo action required. The tracing configuration defaults remain backward compatible.\n\n### For Users With Tracing Enabled\n\n1. **Optional**: If you want to reduce trace overhead in production, add the `samplingRatio` option:\n   ```yaml\n   tracing:\n     enabled: true\n     samplingRatio: 0.1  # Adjust based on your needs\n   ```\n\n2. **Optional**: If you need to support trace propagation between systems, configure multiple propagators:\n   ```yaml\n   tracing:\n     enabled: true\n     propagators:\n       - tracecontext\n       - baggage\n       - jaeger  # Add if integrating with Jaeger systems\n   ```\n\n3. **Restart** your Flipt instance after configuration changes.\n\n### Verification\n\nAfter upgrading, verify tracing is working:\n1. Check Flipt startup logs for any tracing configuration errors\n2. Confirm traces are reaching your trace collector\n3. If sampling is configured, verify that the expected percentage of traces are being collected\n\n## Bug Fixes\n\n- Fixed tracing configuration tests to properly validate new propagator and sampling ratio options\n- Corrected trace resource construction to use latest OpenTelemetry semantic conventions\n\n## Dependencies\n\n- Updated OpenTelemetry semantic conventions to v1.24.0\n- Added support for OpenTelemetry contrib propagators auto-detection (`autoprop`)\n\n## API Changes\n\n### gRPC/REST APIs\n\nNo changes to the public gRPC or REST APIs. This release only enhances observability through improved tracing configuration.\n\n### Configuration Schema\n\nNew fields added to `tracing` configuration:\n- `samplingRatio` (optional, default: 1)\n- `propagators` (optional, default: [\"tracecontext\", \"baggage\"])\n\nFull schema validation is available in `config/flipt.schema.json`.\n\n## Performance Considerations\n\n- **Sampling**: Setting `samplingRatio` to less than 1.0 can significantly reduce trace collection overhead in high-traffic deployments\n- **Propagators**: Adding more propagators has minimal performance impact (evaluated at request time)\n- **Resource Attributes**: Automatic resource collection may add small overhead but provides valuable context in traces\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n### Traces Not Being Collected\n\n- Verify `tracing.enabled: true` in configuration\n- Check that the trace exporter endpoint is reachable\n- Ensure `samplingRatio` is not set to 0\n- Review Flipt logs for tracing initialization errors\n\n### Invalid Propagator Error\n\n- Verify propagator names match the supported list exactly\n- Common mistake: `trace-context` instead of `tracecontext`\n- Check configuration file syntax (YAML indentation)\n\n### High Trace Volume\n\n- Reduce `samplingRatio` to sample fewer traces\n- Example: `samplingRatio: 0.01` samples 1% of traces\n\n## Questions or Issues?\n\nIf you encounter any issues with this release:\n1. This is a backward-compatible release.\n\n## New Features\n\n### Tracing Configuration Enhancements\n\n#### Sampling Ratio Configuration\n- **`tracing.samplingRatio`**: New configuration option to control the fraction of traces to sample.\n  - Type: `number` (float64)\n  - Range: `0.0` to `1.0`\n  - Default: `1` (sample 100% of traces)\n  - Example configuration:\n    ```yaml\n    tracing:\n      enabled: true\n      exporter: jaeger\n      samplingRatio: 0.1  # Sample 10% of traces\n    ```\n  - **Migration Path**: If you upgrade from a previous version and want to reduce trace overhead, set this value to less than 1. For example, `0.1` will sample only 10% of traces.\n\n#### Trace Propagators Configuration\n- **`tracing.propagators`**: New configuration option to specify OpenTelemetry text map propagators for distributed tracing.\n  - Type: `array` of strings\n  - Default: `[\"tracecontext\", \"baggage\"]`\n  - Supported values:\n    - `tracecontext` - W3C Trace Context propagator\n    - `baggage` - W3C Baggage propagator\n    - `b3` - Zipkin B3 Single propagator\n    - `b3multi` - Zipkin B3 Multi propagator\n    - `jaeger` - Jaeger propagator\n    - `xray` - AWS X-Ray propagator\n    - `ottrace` - OpenTracing propagator\n    - `none` - No-op propagator\n  - Example configuration:\n    ```yaml\n    tracing:\n      enabled: true\n      exporter: jaeger\n      propagators:\n        - tracecontext\n        - baggage\n        - jaeger  # Add Jaeger propagation support\n    ```\n  - **Use Case**: Enable multiple propagators when your traces need to be compatible with different trace collection systems or when propagating traces across systems using different standards.\n\n### Enhanced Tracing Resource Information\n\nTracing spans now include more semantic information from OpenTelemetry semantic conventions v1.24.0:\n- **Service Information**: Service name (`flipt`) and version\n- **Container Information**: Container ID, image name, and other container metadata (when running in containers)\n- **Host Information**: Hostname, OS type, and architecture\n- **Runtime Information**: Go runtime version, runtime name, and description\n- **Telemetry SDK Information**: Information about the OpenTelemetry SDK version being used\n- **Environment Variables**: Automatic detection of OTEL environment variables\n\n## Configuration Guide\n\n### Sampling Configuration Example\n\nTo reduce trace overhead in production while maintaining high sampling in development:\n\n```yaml\nversion: \"1.0\"\n\ntracing:\n  enabled: true\n  exporter: jaeger\n  jaeger:\n    host: localhost\n    port: 6831\n  # Sample only 10% of traces in production\n  samplingRatio: 0.1\n  # Use standard W3C propagators\n  propagators:\n    - tracecontext\n    - baggage\n```\n\n### Multi-Propagator Configuration Example\n\nFor integrations with multiple observability systems:\n\n```yaml\ntracing:\n  enabled: true\n  exporter: otlp\n  otlp:\n    endpoint: localhost:4317\n  # Support multiple trace formats\n  propagators:\n    - tracecontext    # W3C standard\n    - baggage         # W3C baggage\n    - jaeger          # Jaeger format\n    - b3multi         # Zipkin format\n```\n\n## Configuration Validation\n\nThe configuration now validates:\n- **Sampling Ratio**: Must be a number between 0 and 1 (inclusive)\n- **Propagators**: Must be valid propagator names from the supported list\n\nInvalid configurations will result in a clear error message at startup.\n\n## Upgrade Guide\n\n### For Users Not Using Tracing\n\nNo action required. The tracing configuration defaults remain backward compatible.\n\n### For Users With Tracing Enabled\n\n1. **Optional**: If you want to reduce trace overhead in production, add the `samplingRatio` option:\n   ```yaml\n   tracing:\n     enabled: true\n     samplingRatio: 0.1  # Adjust based on your needs\n   ```\n\n2. **Optional**: If you need to support trace propagation between systems, configure multiple propagators:\n   ```yaml\n   tracing:\n     enabled: true\n     propagators:\n       - tracecontext\n       - baggage\n       - jaeger  # Add if integrating with Jaeger systems\n   ```\n\n3. **Restart** your Flipt instance after configuration changes.\n\n### Verification\n\nAfter upgrading, verify tracing is working:\n1. Check Flipt startup logs for any tracing configuration errors\n2. Confirm traces are reaching your trace collector\n3.
